Jamison Brereton

122
All Gods
Kakс╣г─лvant Dairghatamasa
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except vir─Бс╕Нr┼лp─Б 5тАУ6
This hymn is divided almost equally between praise and invocation to a variety of gods (vss. 1тАУ6) and a complex d─Бnastuti (vss. 7тАУ15). As is true of all of Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs oeuvre there are many twists and turns along the way. The part devoted to the gods seems to define an early-morning sacrifice in its first verses, especially those calling on Dawn and Night (vs. 2), the Wind as well as Indra (vs. 3), and the A┼Ыvins and Agni (vs. 4), though Rudra and the Maruts (vs. 1), P┼лс╣гan (vs. 5), and, especially, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (vss. 6тАУ7, 9) also appear. An early-morning ritual284 I.122
is appropriate for the following d─Бnastuti, since the priestly gifts (dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs) are distributed then.
The d─Бnastuti is filled with personal names, and, as often, it is difficult to disen tangle the relationships among them. In fact it appears that we may be dealing with competing potential patrons, each praised for a fleeting moment for his generosity until a larger prize from a different patron is in the offing. In verse 12 the poet seems to be inviting this competition, promising to act as a kind of kingmaker for whom ever he gets as patron, and in the difficult verse 13 the poet may be suggesting that patrons with goods to offer are attempting to surpass competing patrons with their largesse. This interpretation remains uncertain, however.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPresent, mild-tempered (priests), the sacrificial viands which you have prepared, to there warm-showering Rudra. I praise him who, with his heroid (followers) as (with shafts) from a quiver, expelled (the asuras) from heaven; and (I praise) the Maruts, (who abide) between heaven and earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mild-tempered: raghu-manyavaс╕е,of light or little anger; from raghu = laghu, light and manyu = anger. The second p─Бda: lit. ‘I have praised of the expeller from heaven with arrows as if from a quiver the Maruts of heaven and earth’

Jamison Brereton

O you of quick fervor [=priests], bring forward your drink, your stalk, your sacrifice for Rudra who grants rewards.
I have praised (him) along with the heroes of the lord of heaven; (I have praised) the Maruts as if aiming at the two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On p─Б╠Бntam see OldenbergтАЩs lengthy n. ad loc. The stem p─Б╠Бnt(a)-, generally read with distracted root syllable, occurs 8x in the RV. As Oldenberg demonstrates, there are most likely two different stems involved: a them. noun p─Б╠Бnta- тАШdrinkтАЩ and the act.

part. of the root aor. of тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ. The noun is the more common (6x), while the part. is most likely found only in vs. 4 of this same hymn (du. p─Б╠Бnt─Б) and as nom. pl.

in IX.98.8 (q.v.). This distribution of forms is found in Lubotsky, with the part. listed under тИЪp─Б (тАШdrinkтАЩ) and the nom. stem p─Б╠Бnta- separate.

The construction of the second hemistich is much discussed, including the function of the instrumentals. See esp. Oldenberg and Renou

In this context тАЬthe lord (├бsura-) of heavenтАЭ is most likely Rudra (see also Hale, Asuras, 75), who is also the gapped object of the verb astoс╣гi: his heroes are his sons, the Maruts mentioned in d.

On iс╣гudhy─Б╠Бand the related verb, see comm. ad I.128.6 and my forthcoming тАЬVedic iс╣гudhy├б- and Oldenberg Avestan i┼бud-, i┼б┼лidiia-: The Aim of Praise.тАЭ In light of my reconsideration of the word family of iс╣гudhy├б- in that article, I now interpr. this vs. somewhat differently from the published translation Instead of taking r├│dasyoс╕е as the target of the aiming expressed by iс╣гudhy─Б╠Б(тАЬas if aiming at the two world-halvesтАЭ), I now take iс╣гudhy─Б╠Бas an independent instrumental adverb of manner, with a dependent тАЬpraiseтАЭ understood: тАЬтАж as if by the aiming (of an arrow of praise).тАЭ The simile particle iva, which here, unusually, does not mark an explicit simile, draws attention to the underlying metaphor of the aiming of praise. This image is especially appropriate for Rudra, a god of course famous as an archer, and the Maruts, who are depicted in

Griffith

SAY, bringing sacrifice to bounteous Rudra, This juice for drink to you whose wrath is fleeting!
With Dyaus the Asura’s Heroes I have lauded the Maruts as with prayer to Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Bringet euren Somatrank als Opfer dem belohnenden Rudra dar, ihr Eiferwilligen! Ich habe ihn mit den Mannen des Asura des Himmels gepriesen; die Marut preise ich, indem ich gleichsam auf Himmel und Erde Anspruch mache.

Grassmann

Bringt, eifervolle, euern Trank, den Soma, als Opfer dar dem holdgesinnten Rudra, Ich preise mit des hohen Himmels Helden die Maruts, wie nach Erd’ und Himmel zielend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnimated by our diversified praise, hasten, Morning and Night, to attend to our first invocation, as a wife (to the first call of her husband); and may the–Dawn, beautiful with the lustre of the (rising) Sun, and robbing like the Sun (her) vast expanse with golden rays, (come to our early rite).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Star─лс╕е = what covers or expands, smoke; the Sun invested or clothed with light, or destructive of foes: ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm hiс╣Гsakaс╕е tejas─Бchanno v─Б ─Аdityaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

It is for Dawn and Night, like two wives, to strengthen the Early
InvocationтАФthe two that are known in many ways:
(the one) like a barren woman wearing a castoff cloak, (the other) with the glory of the sun, lovely to see with her golden (ornaments).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root affiliation of vy├╣ta- is disputed. Witzel Got┼Н (flg. Rau) take it to тИЪv─Б тАШweaveтАЩ and tr. тАШgeflochtenтАЩ; so also Grassmann and (ultimately) Renou (though he vacillates in his n.). Most other tr. to v├н тИЪyu тАШseparateтАЩ. My тАШcast-offтАЩ comes via тАШseparate, i.e., set aside, get rid ofтАЩ. RenouтАЩs тАЬserti (dтАЩ├йtoiles)тАЭ (sertir =тАШto setтАЩ, of jewels) does not seem to have much to do with тАШweaveтАЩ, but supplying тАЬwith starsтАЭ (stс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е) as a play on star─л╠Бс╕е is clever enough to make his interpr. appealing, though I do not in the end accept it. A bejeweled Night does not fit well with her being star─л╠Б- тАШbarrenтАЩ: the contrast is as usual between dazzlingly beautiful Dawn and dreary dark Night. Cf. the black garment Night spreads at the horizon for the Sun in I.115.4. Night does get her chance at ornaments in the one hymn addressed to her, X.127.

Griffith

Strong to exalt the early invocation are Night and Dawn who show with varied aspect.
The Barren clothes her in wide-woven raiment, and fair Morn shines with Surya’s golden splendour.

Geldner

Nacht und Morgen sollen wie zwei Gattinnen den Erstruf erh├╢hen, die vielfach bekannt sind: Die eine wie eine unfruchtbare Frau in ein abgelegtes Gewand gekleidet, die andere mit der Pracht des Surya sch├╢n im Goldschmuck.

Grassmann

Das Fr├╝hgebet zu segnen, wie zwei Hausfraun erscheinen vielfach Nacht und Morgenr├╢the; Geh├╝llt als Jungfrau in gewobnen Mantel die sch├╢ne goldgeschm├╝ckt im Glanz der Sonne.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the circumambient divinity, the wearer of various forms, grant us delight; may the wind, the shedder of rain, grant us delight; do you, Indra and Parvata, sharpen our (intellects), and may all the gods show us favour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Agni = vasarh─Бn, i.e. assuming various vestures (vasa) or forms (g─Бrhapatya and other fires); or, as destroyingthe vesture of the earth–the trees; or, as causing the revolutions of day and night

Jamison Brereton

Let the earth-circling one [=Wind], rising at early morning, invigorate us. Let the Wind, (child?) of the waters, accompanied by bulls, invigorate us. Sharpen us, o Indra and тАЬMountainтАЭ [=IndraтАЩs mace]. Let all the gods then create wide space for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd member of the cmpd vasarh─Б╠Бis taken by Grassmann and Renou as -h├бn-, hence тАШstriking at dawnтАЩ, but a connection with тИЪh─Б тАШchange position, moveтАЩ makes more sense (so Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], tentatively Scarlatta 700). Wind does regularly rise at dawn, but it is hard to conceive that it smites then. This probably requires us to take the underlying form as -h─Б╠Бs, contra the Pp. The 1st member vasar- is only attested here, as a variant to the (likewise secondary) locatival uс╣гar. See Lundquist 2014 (25th UCLA IE Conf., Proceedings). The somewhat better attested vanar- тАШin the woodтАЩ, also found as 1st cmpd member, may have provided the model for the shape of vasar-.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) construe ap─Б╠Бm with vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гanv─Бn as тАЬder Fuhrmann [coachman, teamster] der Gew├дsser,тАЭ while I follow Renou in tentatively supplying тАШchildтАЩ with gen. ap─Б╠Бm on the basis of the next verse, which contains n├бp─Бtam ap─Б╠Бm. Note that elsewhere in the hymn (12b / 13a) an incomplete expression (d├б┼Ыatayasya) is repaired by the fuller form (d├б┼Ыatayasya dh─Бs├йс╕е). I donтАЩt see how тАШpossessing bullsтАЩ would develop to тАШcoachmanтАЩ. In any case, neither of the alternatives makes much sense as a designation of the wind; I do not know why he would be a coachman of the waters, but I also donтАЩt understand why heтАЩd be the child of the waters – perhaps because of the association of wind with rain or because wind blowing over open water is very perceptible? (For another interpr., see Keydana, Inf., 315 n. 126 тАЬder Besitzer der Wasserhengste [water-stallions],тАЭ which seems to split the difference between the тАШbull[s]/male[s]тАЩ of the nom. and the fem. waters in a way not exactly sanctioned by grammar.) The curious dual dvandva indr─Бparvat─Б тАШIndra and MountainтАЩ is found 3x in the RV (I.132.6, III.53.1 as well as here), always in the voc. I interpret the тАШmountainтАЩ as a reference to IndraтАЩs v├бjra-. For other passages with the v├бjra- as тАШmountainтАЩ, see VI.22.6 and VII.104.19, as well as Renou, EVP XVI.117 (ad VII.104.19).

Griffith

Cheer us the Roamer round, who strikes at morning, the Wind delight us, pourer forth of waters!
Sharpen our wits, O Parvata and Indra. May all the Gods vouchsafe to us this favour.

Geldner

Begeistern soll uns der umherfahrende, in der Fr├╝he kommende Vayu, begeistern der Wind, der Fuhrmann der Gew├дsser. Indra und Parvata, feuert ihr uns an! Alle G├╢tter sollen uns dies gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Erfreun soll uns der Sturm, der fr├╝h den Feind schl├дgt, erfreun der Wind, der Regen uns herbeif├дhrt; Es soll uns Indra st├дrken und der Berggott; das m├╢gen alle G├╢tter uns gew├дhren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhenever I, the son of U┼Ыij, worship with my offerings (of food) those two (A┼Ыvins) who eat and drink (of oblations and libations) at (the season) of the world-whitening (dawn); do you, Priests, glorify the grandson of the waters (Agni), and render (the divinities of the day and night) the mothers (as it were) of the man who repeats their praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Trees and shrubs spring up from the moisture of the waters, and fire proceeds from timber;hence, Agni is the grandson of the waters; or son of the waters (Manu, IX. 321)

Jamison Brereton

And it is for (Kakс╣г─лvant), son of U┼Ыij [/the fire-priest], to call for me this glorious pair [=A┼Ыvins], the pursuers (of the oblation), the drinkers, for the whitening (of dawn).
Put forward for yourselves the Child of the Waters [=Agni], forward the two mothers [=kindling sticks] of abundant [?] ─Аyu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is structured like vs. 2, with a nom. subject of a purpose infinitive.

The root тИЪ┼Ыvit is a Dawn word (see I.92.12, 113.15, 124.11, the last in a nearby Kakс╣г─лvant hymn); I wonder if ┼Ыvetan─Б╠Б- is feminine because it’s evoking Dawn as the brightener.

Despite their similarity, with most tr. I take p─Б╠Бntam in 1a and p─Б╠Бnt─Б here as belonging to separate stems, the first to p─Б╠Бnta- тАШdrinkтАЩ, the second to the act. part. to the root aor. of тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ (see disc. above ad v. 1). Immediately preceding vy├бnt─Б can be the clue to its participial identity; for the sequence see I.153.4 (of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa) v─лt├бm p─Бt├бm p├бyas─Б тАж The second hemistich with pr├б vaс╕е тАж kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam echoes 1ab pr├б vaс╕е тАж bharadhvam, though in vs. 1 the verb is further distanced from the clause opening.

r─Бspin├б- is a hopeless hapax, surely related to the likewise hopeless hapax r─Бspir├б- in V.43.14, a passage that also contains a mother (m─Бt├║с╣г pad├й) and ─Бy├│с╕е, though not in the same configuration or meaning as here. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) wisely fail to tr.

Renou: тАШfougueuxтАЩ (fiery, ardent), or, in his notes, тАШbouillantтАЩ (boiling), though without serious argumentation. (For other possibilities see KEWA s.v.; AiG III.215.) Although it is foolhardy even to sketch derivational possibilites, I will toss out several, with no conviction. My tentative tr. тАШabundantтАЩ(?) depends on a possible deformation of reasonably well-attested virap┼Ы├нn- тАШid.тАЩ (beside virap┼Ы├б- тАШabundanceтАЩ) (derived in turn from v─лra-p(a)┼Ыu-, in a well-known and generally accepted etym.).

The initial v├н-, perceived as a preverb, could be lopped off, and the unusual internal cluster -p┼Ы- metathesized and normalized to -sp-, whose order of segments and sibilant type are both more phonologically natural. The apparent vс╣Ыddhi might be like that of m─Б╠Бhina- though they are differently accented. To account for r─Бspir├б- we must assume that r─Бspin├б- was analyzed as containing a -n├б-suffix, for which -r├бwas substituted for no discernible reason. Another even less good possibility, which partly goes back to Bollensen (ZDMG 22; see KEWA s.v., AiG III.215), starts from the fact that in context both r─Бspin├б- and r─Бspir├б- could use an extra syllable. The first member could be analyzed as a y-less genitive *r─Б├бs to ray├н- / r─Бy- тАШwealthтАЩ, compounded with a form of тИЪpi тАШswellтАЩ. (Note that r─Бy├бs regularly shows -s sandhi in syntagms before p: esp. r─Бy├бs p├│с╣гam, but cf. also r─Бy├бs p┼лrdhi.) However, our current understanding of the historical morphology of the тАШwealthтАЩ word makes it well-nigh impossible to get such a -y-less form (since r─Бy├бs тЖР *raHi-╠пas) without a series of arbitrarily constructed analogies. Thus, the second possibility is essentially ruled out, and, insofar as I think itтАЩs worth even thinking about an etymology here, I favor the deformation from virap┼Ы├нn-.

I do not know what role ─Аyu is playing here, as is often the case with this figure.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI, the son of U┼Ыij, address to you (A┼Ыvins) audible praises, in like manner as Ghoс╣г─Б praised you for the removal of her white-tinted (skin); I glorify (gods) the bountiful P┼лс╣гan (associated) with you, and I proclaim the munificence of Agni.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is for (Kakс╣г─лvant), son of U┼Ыij [/the fire-priest], to call the тАЬscreecher,тАЭ the laud, for you as if with a shout, at the attainment of the silvery
one [=soma?].
(Put him [=P┼лс╣гan]?) forward for yourselves, for P┼лс╣гan to give. I would call here AgniтАЩs assemblage of good ones [=gods].

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again the first hemistich has a predicated infinitive, like 2ab, 4ab. In fact the structure is identical to that in 4: au┼Ыij├│ huv├бdhyai# (4b, 5a). But otherwise the verse is difficult to comprehend (as Geldner says in n. 5, тАЬVoll dunkler BeziehungenтАЭ), and tr.

differ considerably. I will not treat them in detail.

The object(s) of huv├бdhyai should first be sorted out: the two acc. ruvaс╣Зy├║m and s├бс╣Гsam. Are the two coreferential and what are their referent(s)? ruvaс╣Зy├║- is a hapax but clearly derived from the denom. (/deverb.?) stem ruvaс╣Зya- (also a hapax) and ultimate from the root тИЪru тАШbellow, roarтАЩ. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes ruvaс╣Зy├║m as a qualifier of ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam, which he treats as a PN (тАЬden lauten ┼Ъaс╣ГsaтАЭ), perhaps standing for N─Бra┼Ыaс╣Гsa. This is not impossible, but given the mysterious ─Бy├│с╕е in 4d and au┼Ыij├бс╕е in both 4b and 5a, I am reminded the phrase u┼Ы├нjaс╕е ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam ─Бy├│с╕е (IV.6.11, V.3.4). In both passages we (SWJ and JPB respectively) take ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam ─Бy├│с╕е тАЬthe laud of ─АyuтАЭ as a designation of Agni; in both we take the form u┼Ы├нjaс╕е as the nom. pl.

designation of a type of priest, who do homage to Agni under this name. Note also that II.31.6 contains ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam u┼Ы├нj─Бm, with the ─Аyus featuring in the next verse (II.31.7b) as makers of hymns. I therefore think that ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam in this verse should be combined with the mysterious ─Бy├│с╕е at the end of the previous verse into a putative underlying phrase *┼Ы├бс╣Гsam ─Бy├│с╕е, referring to Agni, modified by ruvaс╣Зy├║m.

Incomplete phrases straddling verse divisions are found in vss. 3-4 and 12-13 (though in those instances the complete phrase appears in the 2nd vs.); see comm. above on vs. 3. I would thus change the text of the published translation to тАЬIt is for (Kakс╣г─лvant), son of U┼Ыij, to call the bellower, the тАШLaud (of ─Аyu)тАЩ [=Agni], for you.тАЭ Agni can be characterized as тАШbellowing, roaringтАЩ because of the crackling of his flames. The тАЬyouтАЭ are the priests (etc.) on whose behalf Kakс╣г─лvant is acting. Agni was ritually presented in the previous hemistich (4c) under a different epithet, and his тАЬmothersтАЭ (the kindling sticks) in 4d. A тАЬroaringтАЭ Agni would come into being following the kindling about to take place in 4d. An invocation to AgniтАЩs comrades ends this verse (5d). The context thus favors Agni.

The next problem is gh├│с╣гeva. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes this as the fem. PN Ghoс╣г─Б, the erstwhile spinster, found in a nearby Kakс╣г─лvant hymn (I.117.7) where the A┼Ыvins bestowed a husband on her, as well as in the famous sequence of hymns X.39-41 attributed to her (with the patronymic K─Бkс╣г─лvat─л) and her son. Despite the close connection of Kakс╣г─лvant with this Ghoс╣г─Б, I doubt that she figures in the strictly liturgical context here, and those who think she does must assume that Arjuna is the name of her acquired husband, for which there is no evidence. I take the form rather as the old instr. gh├│с╣г─Б to the masc. common noun gh├│с╣гa- тАШshout, cryтАЩ, though I admit the simile seems a bit lame. RenouтАЩs grammatical interpr. is the same as mine; his tr.

тАЬsemblable ├а une rumeur (de guerre)тАЭ is less lame, but even less supported.

n├бс╣Г┼Ы├й occurs twice in the RV, here and in 12b in this hymn, both times preceded by a genitive. There seems no reason not to take it, with Grassmann etc., as the loc. sg. to a stem n├бс╣Г┼Ыa- тАШat/on the attainmentтАЩ construed with the gen. As for ├бrjunasya, lit. тАШsilver(y)тАЩ, I suggest that it refers to soma; cf. с╣Ыj─лс╣г├нn- тАШpossessing the silvery drink [=soma]тАЩ (so Thieme), with the Caland form с╣Ыji- to this same etymon. Unfortunately ├бrjuna- doesnтАЩt elsewhere characterize soma. Nonetheless, the fact that the other occurrence of n├бс╣Г┼Ыe (12b) takes a genitive that also probably refers to soma gives some support to this interpr.

The initial pr├б in c, echoing those in 1a and 4c, suggests that this hemistich has a structure parallel to those two. Hence my тАЬ(put him) forwardтАЭ; other tr. supply other material to complete the clause. The meter of this p─Бda is deficient, lacking three syllables. Various restorations have been suggested (see Oldenberg, Prol. 113 n. 1 [=Engl. tr. 133 n. 3]; Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition metrical notes ad loc.). Oldenberg (Prol.) suggests an impv. like arcata or g─Бyata, noting the structural similarity to 4c, but in the Noten he suggests that the metrical irregularity of Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs I.120 might indicate that the text here is correctly transmitted and that the meter must be taken as is. It is certainly difficult to see how a trisyllabic verb form would have simply got dropped here.

I do not understand how P┼лс╣гan comes to be named in this august divine company, and I wonder if the abbreviated meter of this p─Бda has something to do with the dedicand: the only hymns addressed solely to P┼лс╣гan in the RV, VI.53-58, consist entirely of dimeter hymns save for the last. The 8-syllable p─Бda here might signal his more humble stature.

vas├║t─Бti- is another word that occurs in the RV only here and in vs. 12 of this same hymn. Its formation is of course transparent, but its meaning is less so. Most take it as a true abstract to v├бsu- тАШgood(s)тАЩ, but with a slight twist to тАШgenerosityтАЩ (Freigebigkeit). But the lexeme ├бcha тИЪvac seems to be a technical ritual term for тАШinviteтАЩ (cf. ├бchokti- and the later priestly title acch─Бv─Бka-) with gods as the object.

Grassmann suggests the meaning тАШSchaar der Guten, d.h. der G├╢tterтАЩ for the occurrence in vs. 12 (but not this one), which I have adopted for both instances. It would be equiv. to dev├бt─Бti- тАШassemblage/conclave of godsтАЩ. The p─Бda would then refer to the group of divinities that Agni regularly conveys to the sacrifice.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa, hear these my invocations, and moreover listen to those (that are) everywhere (uttered) in the chamber of sacrifice; and may Sindhu, the renowned bestower of wealth, hear us, (fertilizing our) broad fields with water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sindhu: deity presiding over water, jal─Бbhim─Бni devaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Hear these calls of mine, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, and hear them in your seat on all sides.
Let the one who grants the gift of hearing, who hears well, hear usтАФthe Sindhu River with her waters who provides good lands.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This last verse before the d─Бnastuti is free of the manifold difficulties that clot the first five verses of the hymn, but it is not devoid of Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs poetic flourishes. Note first the play on тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhearтАЩ, which reaches a climax in p─Бda c: ┼Ыr├│tu naс╕е ┼Ыr├│turatiс╕е su┼Ыrotuс╕е. What is particularly clever here is that though the p─Бda contains three forms ┼Ыr├│tu, the first is completely different from the second two: it is the 3rd sg. act. root aor. impv., while the other two belong to the nominal stem ┼Ыr├│tuand are 1st and 2nd compound members respectively. The p─Бda has only 10 syllables, with a likely rest after ┼Ыr├│tu naс╕е, which would call attention to the phonological identity / morphological difference.

The phrase vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е s─лm occurs 5x in the RV; I have discussed this formula at length elsewhere (тАЬRigvedic vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е s─лm, or why syntax needs poeticsтАЭ, M├нr Curad, Fs. C. Watkins [edd. J. Jasanoff, H.C. Melchert, and L. Oliver], 1998, pp. 291-300).

The two occurrences in Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs oeuvre (I.116.20 and here) ring changes on the basic formula in his usual deft and unexpected ways. I will not reproduce the entire discussion, but summarize the main points. Four of the five passages (all but this one) concern the theme тАЬsurrounding,тАЭ marked by p├бri + VERB. In three of these (all but the two Kakс╣г─лvant examples) the object is the two worlds / heaven and earth. In I.20 it is the subject (the A┼Ыvins), not the object, that is dual. In other words, Kakс╣г─лvant has transformed the underlying formula by transferring the abstract grammatical category DUAL from one of the arguments of the verb to the other.

This analysis of I.116.20 is necessary to understand the more attenuated – and more radical – instantiation of the formula found in our verse here. As in I.116.20 the DUAL that is inherent in the formula surfaces on the subject, here Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, but the тАЬsurroundingтАЭ motif is not present, except in vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е тАШon all sidesтАЩ itself, which seems to have no semantic connection with the rest of its clause. Why is it here? Because it is crossed with a different formula through surface phonological similarity. Consider the word s├бdane in the same p─Бda, which has connections with another RVic formula. The phrase тАЬin the seat of VivasvantтАЭ occurs five times in the RV (I.53.1, III.34.7, III.51.3, X.12.7, X.75.1), twice as p─Бda-final s├бdane viv├бsvataс╕е# (I.53.1, X.75.1). This provides an almost perfect phonological scrambling of our p─Бda ending.(In fact, according to Oldenberg [Noten, ad loc.], Ludwig suggested emending vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е to vivasvataс╕е [no accent given].) s├бdane viv├бsvataс╕е# s├бdane vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е s─лm# Thus our phrase may have been employed in order to evoke the other formula, which is a kenning for тАЬder Opferplatz," so Geldner ad I.53.1. Thus Kakс╣г─лvant deftly marries the grammatical deep structure (the dual) of the vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е s─лm formula with the surface phonology of s├бdane viv├бsvataс╕е in a way that allows the semantics of both to be alluded to. (Perhaps an appreciation of the formulaic manipulations involved here would have led Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions) to reconsider his assessment of this verse with its тАЬhysterical repetition of the root ┼ЫruтАЭ as тАЬsecondary clap-trap.тАЭ) I do not understand why the Sindhu is esp. gifted with hearing.

Griffith

Hear, Mitra-Varuna, these mine invocations, hear them from all men in the hall of worship.
Giver of famous gifts, kind hearer, Sindhu who gives fair fields, listen with all his waters!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI praise you, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, for your gift of numerous cattle to the Pajra, and (from those praises) may abundant food (proceed). May (the gods), bestowing nourishment on me, come quickly unimpeded, (each) in his famous and favourite car.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kakс╣г─лvat, of the family of Pajra; ┼Ыrutarathe priyarathe (mayi): ‘on me possessing a famous car’

Jamison Brereton

This gift of yours is to be praised, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa. Having received hundreds of cows among the Pr╠еkс╣гay─Бmas: Pajra,
┼Ъrutaratha, Priyaratha, they [=priests and poets] immediately came to prosperity, upon penning them in.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The transition between the All God portion of the hymn and the d─Бnastuti is eased by verbal repetition: Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who were the last gods invoked (6ab), are again called on here, though in opposite order and not in a dvandva but in individual vocatives (varuс╣Зa mitra versus 6a mitr─Бvaruс╣З─Б). Independent r─Бt├нс╕е picks up the 2nd cmpd member in ┼Ыr├│tu-r─Бtiс╕е (6c) and the PN ┼Ыrut├бratha- (7c) also echoes ┼Ыr├│tu-r─Бtiс╕е.

The locc. pajr├й / ┼Ыrut├бrathe priy├бrathe mark these men as givers, which makes some trouble, since Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs family seems to be called Pajra (quite possibly in the next verse and in I.126.4-5) and Kakс╣г─лvant himself pajriy├б- (I.116.7, 117.6, 120.5). Nonetheless, grammar canтАЩt be gainsaid, and they must be patrons here. See GeldnerтАЩs n. 7bc for attempts to reconcile the discrepancies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The passively used 3rd sg. stuс╣г├й (7a), stuс╣гe (8a) contrast in function with the great majority of stuс╣г├й / stuс╣гe forms, which are 1st sg. and тАЬactiveтАЭ in sense (тАЬI (will) praiseтАЭ). This rare usage may be mediated through the perception of the accented forms as infinitives; see disc. ad X.22.1.

Griffith

Praised, Mitra, Varuna! is your gift, a hundred cows to the Prksayamas and the Pajra.
Presented by car-famous Priyaratha, supplying nourishment, they came directly.

Geldner

Gelobt wird diese Gabe vor euch, Mitra und Varuna: Als sie Hunderte von K├╝hen bei den Priksayama┬┤s, bei Pajra,Srutaratha bekamen, sind sie gegangen, indem sie sofort ihren Viehzuwachs einhegten.

Grassmann

Gepriesen wird, o Mitra-Varuna, vor euch diese Gabe; [ich empfing] von den Prikschajama’s und dem Padschra hundert Rinder; die von dem wagenber├╝hmten Prijaratha geschenkten, Nahrung in sich enthaltenden [Rinder] sind mir an demselben Tage zugekommen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI laud the treasures of that opulent (assemblyof the gods); may we, men who (are blessed) with excellent descendants, partake of them together; the assembly conferring upon the Pajras abundant food, has been my benefactor, and has made me the master of horses and chariots.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mahimaghasya r─Бdhas = the riches of that, or of him, who or which ispossessed of great wealth; i.e., deva-saс╣Еgha, the assembly or company of the gods; the assembly: the text ahs: jano yaс╕е, the man who; ya┼Ыca deva saс╣Еghaс╕е, the assembly of the gods which

Jamison Brereton

The largesse of him who offers great bounty is to be praised. Together might we, having good heroes, win (that) of Nahus, who for the Pajras is the man providing prizewinning mares and for me is the patron (of largesse) consisting of horses and chariots.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See Oldenberg on this vs. I follow him in taking cd as a single rel. cl. hanging off Nahus in b, rather than a rel. cl. / main cl. structure. The uncertainty about the relationships of the various named patrons makes any interpr. tentative. See published

introduction.

Griffith

Praised is the gift of him the very wealthy: may we enjoy it, men with hero children:
His who hath many gifts to give the Pajras, a chief who makes me rich in cars and horses.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe mman who does you wrong, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who injures you in any way, who does not present you with oblations, contracts for himself sickness in his heart; but he who, performing worship, (celebrates it) with praises.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Akс╣гс╣Зay─Б dhruk: cakreс╣Зa, m─Бrgeс╣Зa druhyati, offends by a wheel, or a way; this is the equivalent of anyath─Б prakareс╣Зa, in another manner; yakс╣гmam hс╣Ыdaye nidhatte:he plural ces or deposits consumption in the heart; but yakс╣гma = vy─Бdhi, sickness in genitive ral; a reference, perhaps, to the sense of mortification experienced by those who neglect the gods on observing the blessings which recompense devotion.

Jamison Brereton

A man whoтАЩs a liar, a crooked liar who presses (soma thatтАЩs) like water for you two, o Mitra and Varuс╣Зa,
he himself installs a wasting disease in his own heart, while the truthful man gains his object through his oblations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This cautionary example of what happens to men who cheat the gods of proper offerings is clearly meant to warn stingy patrons.

Note the echo between the openings of b #ap├│ and d #─Б╠Бpa, which are entirely distinct grammatically. As for the latter, as K├╝mmel also notes, various forms of the perfect of тИЪ─Бp have presential value.

Griffith

The folk, O Mitra-Varuna, who hate you, who sinfully hating pour you no libations,
Lay in their hearts, themselves, a wasting sickness, whereas the righteous gaineth all by worship.

Geldner

Der unredliche Mann, der euch, Mitra und Varuna, hinterlistig den Soma wie Wasser bereitet, der bringt sich selbst die Auszehrung ins Herz, w├дhrend der rechttuende mit seinem Opfer Erfolg hat.

Grassmann

Der feindselige, ohne Ursach hassende Mensch, welcher euch, o Mitra-Varuna, nicht Tr├дnke braut, der zieht selbst in sein Innres die Krankheit hinein, w├дhrend der fromme durch Opfer Erf├╝llung [seiner W├╝nsche] erlangt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe, borne by well-trained horses, endowed with surpassing strength, renowned above men, munificent in gifts, moves a hero, ever undaunted in all combats, (even) against mightymen.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He, spurred by wondrous power, is more forceful than proud Nahus, and his fame is sung by men.
He whose gifts have been set loose drives as a pumped-up runner,
always the champion in all battles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner refuses to tr. d├бс╣Гsuj┼лta-. Renou тАЬayant ├йt├й m├╗ (comme) par miracle,тАЭ clearly connecting it with d├бс╣Гsas- тАШwondrous powerтАЩ, etc.; my tr. makes the same connection. The stem d├бс╣Гsu- is probably also found in d├бс╣Гsu-patni- (IV.19.7), though this is disputed. Witzel Got┼Н tr. d├бс╣Гsuj┼лta- тАЬals Heimkehrer,тАЭ with the 1st member the loc. pl. of d├бm- тАШhouseтАЩ – so, more literally, тАШin die H├дuser eilendтАЩ. This is clever, and the two independent uses of d├бс╣Гsu, both nearby (I.134.4, 141.4), do seem to be that loc. pl. However, j┼лta- means тАШsped, spurred onтАЩ and the fairly numerous compds in which it occurs have a 1st member that provides impetus (cf., e.g., v─Б╠Бtaj┼лta- тАШwind-spedтАЩ); тАШsped into the houseтАЩ sounds more like an act of cowardice or retreat than of triumph.

b─Бс╕╖hasс╣Ы╠Бtv─Б in c is even more problematic (though Geldner does tr. it: тАЬgeht er [y─Бti] festes GangesтАЭ). Independent sс╣Ы╠е╠Бtvan- means тАШrunning, streamingтАЩ; b─Бс╕╖ha- means тАШthick, squeezedтАЩ, to тИЪbaс╣Гh. Although it would of course be possible to attenuate that meaning to тАШfirm, powerfulтАЩ, I think that Kakс╣г─лvant, by using this unusual compound, and esp. the unusual 1st member, had something more precise in mind than a firm stride – esp. in a d─Бnastuti, where slang is most at home. I have therefore used the Engl. idiom тАШpumped upтАЩ (approximating the тАШsqueezed, denseтАЩ sense of the Skt.), which is defined by an online dict. (http://www.thefreedictionary.com) as тАЬtense with excitement and enthusiasm as from a rush of adrenaline,тАЭ with the following example: “we were really pumped up for the race.”

Griffith

That man, most puissant, wondrously urged onward, famed among heroes, liberal in giving,
Moveth a warrior, evermore undaunted in all encounters even with the mighty.

Geldner

Dieser ……..ist st├дrker noch als der m├дchtige Nahus; sein Ruhm wird von den M├дnnern gepriesen. Gaben austeilend geht er festen Ganges, in allen K├дmpfen immerdar ein Held.

Grassmann

Er geht hin zu den gewaltigen Genossen mit Wunderkraft eilend, der k├╝hnste der M├дnner, dessen Ruhm hoch gepriesen wird, dessen Gaben sich reichlich ergiessen, kr├дftig einhereilend, stets ein Held in allen Schlachten.

Elizarenkova

тАЬRoyal bestowers of delight, listen to the invocation of (your) undying worshipper, and then come hither, that you who traverse the sky may be propitiated by the greatness of the (sacrificial) wealth presented to you by the sacrificer, who acknowledges no other protector.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amс╣Ыtasya nahuс╣гo havam sureс╕е = ─Бhav─Бnam amarс╣Зasya stotr─Бdiprerakasya manuс╣гyasya mama, the invocation of me, a mortal, instrumental gating praises and the like, not dying. Alternative rendering: the invocation of the immortal (deity) by me, a mortal worshipper

Jamison Brereton

Now then, as you go to the call of Nahus the patron, o gladdening kings of immortality, hear
what largesse of Nabhoj┼л and of Nirava there is for the possessor of the chariot to proclaim in its greatness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The dual part. gm├бnt─Б of p─Бda a does not match the pl. impv. ┼Ыr├│t─Б of b nor the pl. voc. r─Бj─Бnaс╕е in the same p─Бda. Drawing the distinction did not seem worth it in the published translation – which would have to be something like тАЬas you two go тАж, (do all of you) hear тАжтАЭ The number discrepancy is generally (and in my opinion correctly) interpreted as first a reference to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa and then to the ─Аdityas as a group. M+V were prominent earlier (vss. 6-7, 9; see also 15c, the final vs.) and in fact in vs. 7 ushered in the d─Бnastuti. The plural phrase in b is used precisely of the three principal ─Аdityas, including explicitly M+V, in X.93.5: t├й gh─Б r─Б╠Бj─Бno amс╣Ы╠Бtasya mandr─Б╠Б, aryam─Б╠Бmitr├│ v├бruс╣Зaс╕е тАж This parallel also shows that ScarlattaтАЩs clever idea (171, followed by Witzel Got┼Н) to construe amс╣Ы╠Бtasya with the verb ┼Ыr├│t─Б cannot be correct.

In c Oldenberg takes the hapaxes nabhoj┼л╠Б- and nirav├б- in full lexical value, rather than as PN, and, at least acdg. to Mayr. (PN, svv.), this remains a live possibility.

However, in the d─Бnastuti context names are more likely, though they can be speaking names. That -j┼л- echoes -j┼лta- in 10a and -rav├б- echoes ruvaс╣Зy├║- in 5a (assuming an analysis ni-rav├б- with Oldenberg, rather than nir-av├б- with Grassmann) is presumably no accident: puns on personal names are a standard RVic poetic device.

Griffith

Come to the man’s, the sacrificer’s calling: hear, Kings of Immortality, joy-givers!
While ye who speed through clouds decree your bounty largely, for fame, to him the chariot rider.

рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрдЪ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods have declared: we confer present vigour upon the worshipper (who invokes us) to partake of the (ibation). May all (the gods) in whom splendour and riches abound, bestow (abundant) food at (solemn) sacrifices.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Da┼Ыataya = a decade: food, by which the vigour of the ten senses is augment; or Soma offered in ten ladles. Alternative rendering of the second p─Бda: May all the gods partake of the abundant food (or Soma) at those sacrifices in which the priests are the distributors of the riches of copious libations

Jamison Brereton

тАЬWhichever patron (we belong to), we shall establish him as a force,тАЭ so did they say on the attainment of ten-part (gushing [=soma?]).
The brilliant things in which the assemblage of good ones [=gods] finds enjoymentтАФlet them all [=gods] gain (them) as their victory prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. differs from most (though it is closest to OldenbergтАЩs). There are two major reasons for the different interpr. in p─Бda a: 1) most take dh─Бma as part of the rel. cl., but this is impossible because the verb is unaccented; 2) most take ┼Ы├бrdham as a reference to the Marut troop. This is, of course, its standard use, but in this hymn it should first be interpreted in conjunction with ┼Ы├бrdhastara- тАШmore forcefulтАЩ in 10b, where it qualifies an unnamed patron. Here we want to establish our patron (s┼лr├н-) as such a force. In my interpr. the rel. cl. is a nominal cl. consisting only of y├бsya s┼лr├йс╕е, in which *vay├бm (or *sm├бs[i]) can be supplied (from the 1st pl. inherent in dh─Бma), as an expression of possession: тАЬof which patron (we) [are],тАЭ i.e., тАЬwho is (our) patron.тАЭ Cf. the type VIII.92.32 tv├бm asm─Б╠Бkaс╣Г t├бva smasi тАЬyou are ours; we are yours.тАЭ The speakers in b are the poet(s) and priest(s). The gen. d├б┼Ыastayasya тАШtenfoldтАЩ must be interpreted in light of the fuller expression d├б┼Ыastayasya dh─Бs├йс╕е in 13a тАЬtenfold gush,тАЭ probably a kenning for soma, though there is no agreement on its sense. The fact that the fuller expression serves as a complement of the verb m├бnd─Бmahe, a standard soma verb, in 13a supports this identification. The тАШtenfoldтАЩ characterization is not clear; Oldenberg plausibly suggests that it refers to the number of servings to be divided among that number of priests.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and possibly Renou take cd as a resumption of the direct speech of p─Бda a. This is not impossible, but the 3rd persons of c and d have no clear referents in a.

I take dyumn─Б╠Бni in c as a fronted object of sanvantu in d, more or less following Oldenberg This technically makes y├йс╣гu тАж r─Бr├бn appear to be an embedded rel.

cl., which IтАЩm afraid I will just have to live with.

As indicated in the comm. to vs. 5, I take vas├║t─Бti- here as a reference to the collectivity of good ones, namely gods. I then take the pl. v├н┼Ыve opening the next p─Бda as referring also to the gods. In this Vi┼Ыve Dev─Бс╕е hymn, the poet cleverly makes reference to them here in this off-kilter expression, with dev─Б╠Бс╕е suppressed and anticipated by the sg. vas├║t─Бti-. (The full expression is found in 3d.) My only reservation about this interpr. is that in a d─Бnastuti it should be mortals who are doing the winning, and certainly the phrase prabhс╣Ыth├й┼Ыu v─Б╠Бjam тАЬthe victory prize in the foraysтАЭ fits a mortal context better. I might then modify my tr. to remove the bracketed тАЬ[=gods]тАЭ and leave the identity of the subject open. It may in fact be that the two objects dyumn─Б╠Бni and v─Б╠Бjam will be won by gods and mortals respectively, and v├н┼Ыve refers to both, hence тАЬlet all (the gods) win the brilliant things in which the assemblage of good ones takes pleasure, and let all (the mortals) win the victory prize at the forays.тАЭ

Griffith

Vigour will we bestow on that adorer whose tenfold draught we come to taste, so spake they.
May all in whom rest splendour and great riches obtain refreshment in these sacrifices.

Ein Patron, dessen bekannte Marutschar wir bilden wollen", so sprachen sie bei dem Empfang der zehnfachen Speise, “bei denen Glanz und Freigebigkeit gern verweilen m├╢ge, sie alle sollen bei den Unternehmungen Gewinn davontragen!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe rejoice tha tfor the satisfaction of the ten (organs of sense), the (priests) bearing the twice five (ladles of) sacrificial food, proceed (to the altar). What can Iс╣гс╣нa┼Ыva, (what can) Iс╣гс╣нara┼Ыmi, (what can) those who are now lords of the earth, achieve (with respect) to the leaders of men, the conquerors of their foes?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Da┼Ыataya = da┼Ыatayasya dh─Бse, i.e. the ten indriyas,or organs of sense; twice five: ten ladles by the Soma is thrown on the fire; or, the ten articles offered in sacrifices, such as honey,butter, curds, milk, water, grain, offered to fire at the a┼Ыvamedha; whaat can those: what can the princes who are named, or any other princes, do against those who enjoy the protection of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Let us find elation in the ten-part gush (of soma?), when the twice five [=fingers?] come, bringing foods.
The one providing desirable horses, the one providing desirable reins, and these masters (of goods)тАФare they heading straight toward the men to surpass (them)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the phrasal repair of 12b d├б┼Ыatayasya by d├б┼Ыastayasya dh─Бs├йс╕е see comm. vss. 3, 5, and 12.

The тАЬtwice fiveтАЭ in p─Бda b may be the fingers, as I suggest (almost the default identification in a RVic ritual context), or the number of priests, indirectly conveyed by the tenfold soma of 12b and 13a. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes the тАЬtwice fiveтАЭ as directly characterizing ├бnn─Б: the twice five foods.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and Renou take iс╣гс╣н─Б╠Б┼Ыvaс╕е and iс╣гс╣н├бra┼Ыmiс╕е as PNs of patrons. (Actually Renou omits the first, presumably inadvertently.) I also take them as referring to patrons but with full lexical value: the one who has тАЬdesirable horsesтАЭ and тАЬdesirable reinsтАЭ [latter probably a stand-in for тАЬchariotsтАЭ] to offer. That тАЬthose showing masteryтАЭ (─л┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бsaс╕е) are patrons is strongly suggested by I.141.3, where that participle modifies s┼лr├бyaс╕е тАШpatronsтАЩ. The Saс╣Гhit─Б text t├бruс╣гa is analyzed by the Pp. as t├бruс╣гaс╕е, which could be a gen. with ─л┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бsaс╕е (so Grassmann, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) or nom. pl. (so Geldner). Oldenberg suggests that it could also be read as dat. t├бruс╣гe, against the Pp., which is how I take it. I then interpr. nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn as referring not to the singers (so Geldner et al.) but to still other patrons with whom they are competing to provide the best recompense to the singers.

Griffith

We will rejoice to drink the tenfold present when the twicefive come bearing sacred viands.
What can he do whose steeds and reins are choicest? These, the all-potent, urge brave men to conquest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay all the gods favour us with a person n decorated with golden earrings and jewel necklace; may the venerable (company of the deities) be propitiated by the praises issuing (from the mouth of the worshipper); may our offerings be acceptable to them, and (may they be plural ased) with both (our praises and offerings).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Arс╣Зas = r┼лpe, form; i.e., a son; may they be plural ased with both = may they reward us in both worlds; the text has only ubhayeс╣гu, in both

Jamison Brereton

The тАЬfloodтАЭ with golden ears and bejeweled necksтАФlet all the gods make it wide for us.
Let the ruddy ones [=Dawns?], coming here in an instant to the songs of the stranger, find pleasure in both of us [=singers and patrons].

Jamison Brereton Notes

As is recognized by all, the flood (├бrс╣Зaс╕е) is the herd of gift cows, whose constant turbulent motion must have suggested the metaphor. Accentless maс╣Зigr─лvam Oldenberg considers a тАЬmonstrosityтАЭ due to faulty transmission. It must be a bahuvr─лhi like immediately preceding h├нraс╣Зyakarс╣Зam, and I now wonder if the phrase h├нraс╣Зyakarс╣Зam maс╣Зigr─лvam actually represents a dvandva consisting of two bahuvr─лhis (тАШpossessing golden ears and ornamented necksтАЩ), which could account for the single accent. The geminate m across the compound boundary (-karс╣Зam maс╣Зi-) might have been redactionally introduced from *-karс╣Зa-maс╣Зi-). The first members of the two compounds h├нraс╣Зya- and maс╣Зi- are the constituents of the phrase h├нraс╣Зyena maс╣З├нn─Б in I.33.8, on which see my extensive discussion in тАЬA Golden Amulet in Vedic and AvestanтАЭ (Ged. H. P. Schmidt).

P─Бda b is repeated verbatim from 3d, but because it has an object (the flood) it has a slightly different sense from there.

The reason for the doubled ─Б╠Бin c is not clear to me.

c─Бkantu is taken, plausibly, as haplologized from *c─Бkanantu. See, most recently, K├╝mmel (131).

Griffith

The sea and all the Deities shall give us him with the golden ear and neck bejewelled.
Dawns, hasting to the praises of the pious, be pleased with us, both offerers and singers.

Geldner

Die wogende Masse, die Gold an den Ohren und Juwelen am Hals tr├дgt, die sollen uns alle G├╢tter g├╢nnen. Die Morgenr├╢ten sollen alsbald zu dem Lobe des hohen Herrn erscheinend an beiden teilen von uns ihre Freude haben.

Grassmann

Die wallende Schar (?) mit Goldschmuck am Ohr und Perlen am Halse, die m├╢gen uns alle G├╢tter segnen; die Morgenr├╢then, herkommend zu den Liedern des frommen, m├╢gen Gefallen haben an uns, den S├дngern und den Spendern.

English translation:

тАЬThe four (silly) sons of Ma┼Ыar’┼Ы─Бra, the three of the victorious monarch ─Аyavasa (annoy) me. Let your spacious and bright-rayed chariot, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, blaze (before them) like the sun (filling them with fear).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъi┼Ыvaс╕е = ┼Ыi┼Ыavaс╕е, infant, i.e. infantile, childish

Jamison Brereton

The four youngтАЩuns [=foals?] of Ma┼Ыar┼Ы─Бra and the three of King ─Аyavasa, the victorious (come) to me.
Your chariot, o Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, with its long front, with hands as its guiding rope, has shone like the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation, there should be a comma after тАЬvictorious.тАЭ What verb to supply in ab seems up to the interpreter.

I do not understand the image in sy┼л╠Бma-gabhasti- тАШwith hands as its guiding ropeтАЩ.

Griffith

Four youthful sons of Masarsara vex me, three, of the king, the conquering Ayavasa.
Now like the Sun, O Varuna and Mitra, your car hath shone, long-shaped and reined with splendour.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЧреБрдг, рдХрд░реНрдо, рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рд╕реЗ рдирд┐рдпрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдЬрди рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдг рдФрд░ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдо рддрдерд╛ рд╕реЗрдирд╛, рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡рд╣ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЗ рддреБрд▓реНрдп рдХреАрд░реНрддреНрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд╢реЛрднрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рее резрел реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдзрд░реНрдо рдХреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣реЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдПрдХрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ резреиреи рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдмрд╛рдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреАрд╕рд░рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдкреВрд░рд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛ рдпреЛ рд╡рд╛рдВ рд░рдердГ рд╕ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ рдпрд╕реНрдп рдорд╢рд░реНрд╢рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд╕рд╕реНрдп рдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдгреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╕реНрдпреВрдордЧрднрд╕реНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реВрд░реЛ рдд рд░рдереЛрд╜рджреНрдпреМрддреН рддрдерд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдкреНрд╕рд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ рд╕ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣реЗрддреН рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдГ) рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдорд╛рд╢реНрдЪ (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рдорд╢рд░реНрд╢рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп) рдпреЛ рдорд╢рд╛рдиреН рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреН рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдиреН рд╢реГрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рд╣рд┐рдирд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдпред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкреГрд╖реЛрджрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдкрджрд╕реНрдп рд░реБрдЧрд╛рдЧрдордГред (рд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ) рд╢рд╛рд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ (рддреНрд░рдпрдГ) рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд┐рдирдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рдЖрдпрд╡рд╕рд╕реНрдп) рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реАрдХрд╕реНрдп (рдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдгреЛрдГ) рдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓рд╕реНрдп (рд░рдердГ) рдпрд╛рдирдореН (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛) рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреНрд╡рд░реМ (рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдкреНрд╕рд╛рдГ) рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛ рдмреГрд╣рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рдкреНрд╕рд╛рдГ рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдпреЛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ (рд╕реНрдпреВрдордЧрднрд╕реНрддрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдореВрд╣рдХрд┐рд░рдгрдГ (рд╕реВрд░рдГ) рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдЕрджреНрдпреМрддреН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЛ рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рдЧреБрдгрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рддреЛ рдирд┐рдпрддрд╛ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдорд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рдХреАрд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрд╢реЛрднрд┐рддреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее резрел реердЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдмреЛрдзреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЧреБрдг рдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢рд╛рд╕рд┐рдд рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд▓реЛрдХ рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рддрд╕реЗрдЪ рдЪрд╛рд░ рд╡рд░реНрдг рд╡ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдо рдЖрдгрд┐ рд╕реЗрдирд╛, рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛, рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рддреЛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐рдорд╛рди рд╡ рд╕реБрд╢реЛрднрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддреЛ. рее резрел рее
